Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Performing Obligatory Acts During Prohibited Times: Valid but Disliked
Ruling with proof: obligatory acts in prohibited times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that obligatory acts performed during the three prohibited times are valid (sahih) but makruh tahrimi, and apply this ruling to specific examples like funeral prayer and sajdat al-tilawah.

Core Idea
Obligatory acts override time prohibitions: valid but disliked.

The three prohibited times for prayer (sunrise, zenith, sunset) generally forbid voluntary prayer. But what if an obligatory act, like a funeral prayer or a prostration of recitation, becomes due? The Hanafi school teaches that such acts are valid but carry a degree of dislike (karahah tahrimi). This lesson unpacks the reasoning, evidence, and practical applications of this important fiqh principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited times and applicable acts
Name the three times when prayer is generally forbidden (sunrise, zenith, sunset). Then identify which acts are considered obligatory and thus subject to this ruling: funeral prayer (salat al-janazah), prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah), and the current day's Asr prayer when the sun is setting.
The prohibition is for voluntary (nafl) prayers; obligatory acts have a different status.
2
Understand the ruling: validity with dislike
State the ruling: the obligatory act is valid (sahih) but disliked (makruh tahrimi). The validity comes from the obligation (wujub) which takes precedence over the time prohibition. The dislike is due to performing the act in a forbidden time, making it sinful if done without necessity.
Karahah tahrimi means it is close to haram; the act is valid but the person earns sin unless there is a valid excuse.
3
Analyze the evidence (dalil)
Examine the hadith of Uqbah ['Three things are not to be delayed: prayer when it is due, funeral when it arrives, and a woman who finds a suitable match'] which commands immediate performance. This overrides the general prohibition of prayer in these times. The obligation to perform the act is a stronger cause.
The dalil is a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut), so it yields a zanni ruling, but it is accepted in the school.
4
Apply to specific cases and differences
Apply the ruling to: funeral prayer at sunrise (valid with karahah), sajdat al-tilawah at sunset (immediately performed), and the current day's Asr near sunset (valid with karahah due to delay). Also note that voluntary prayers begun in these times should be cut off and made up later, per the stronger view in zahir al-riwayah.
The text addresses a difference: some say cut off nafl, others say continue with dislike. The preferred view is to cut off.

ويصح أداء ما وجب فيها مع الكراهة كجنازة حضرت، وسجدة آية تُليت فيها. كما صح عصر اليوم عندَ الغُروب، معَ الكراهة. والأوقاتُ الثَّلاثةُ.
فائدة: قال في ( القنية وغيرها كسالى العوام إذا صلوا الفجر وقت الطلوع، لا ينكر عليهم، لأنهم لو منعوا، يتركونها أصلاً ظاهراً، ولو صلوها تصح عند أصحاب الحديث، والأداء الجائز عنــد البعض أولى من الترك. (وَيَصُحُ أدَاء مَا وَجَبَ فِيْهَا ، أي الأوقات الثلاثة، لكن (مَـعِ الكَرَاهَةِ)، في ظاهر الرواية، لا كما ظنه البعض، فنفاها ومَثَّلَ لما يجب فيها بقوله (كَجَنَازَةٍ حَضَرَتْ)، أما كراهة الصلاة عليها، فلما تقدم من حديث عقبة ) ، وأما الصحة فلوجوبها بالحضور، لـكـن قــال في معراج الدراية» عن « التحفة » : الأفضل في صلاة الجنازة، أن يؤديها فيها إذا حضرت، لقولـه عليـه الصلاة والسلام: «ثلاث لا يؤخرنَ » (۲) منها الجنازة إذا حضرت. (و) كذا (سجدة آيةٍ تُليت فيها)، أي الأوقات الثلاثة، ونافلة شرع فيها في وقت منها، أو نذر أن يصلي فيها، تجـوز مــع الكـراهـة. والأفضل قطع ما شرع فيه، في ظاهر الرواية، ويقضيه في وقت كامل، لأن الوقت في حقها سبب الوجوب، لا شرط للأداء، بل الأداء وجب مطلقاً، فلا يتقيد بوقت يفوت به، وقيل: يخرج عن عهدته، إذا قضاه في وقت مكروه، وإن كان آثماً، لأن وجوبه لضرورة صيانة المؤدى عن البطلان ليس غير، وهي تحصل مع نقصانه، وقيل: لا يصح الشروع متنفلاً فيها، كالفرائض، لإفادة الدليل المنع مطلقاً دون عدم الصحة في بعضها بخصوصه، وإلا يلزم اختلاف معنى اللفظ الواحد بشيئين مراديــن لا على سبيل الكناية، (كَمَا صَحَ عَصْرُ اليوم) بأدائه ( عندَ الغُروب)، لبقاء سببه، وهو الجزء المتصل به الأداء من الوقت (مَعَ الكَرَاهَةِ؛ للتأخير المنهي عنه، لا لذات الوقت، وقيدنا بعـصـر الـيـوم، لأن عصر أمس لا يصح في حال تغير الشمس من اليوم، لإضافة السببية بخروج الوقت إلى جميعه، وليس مكروهاً، فلا يتأدى في مكروه. وإذا أسلم الكافر عند الاصفرار، ولم يصل، ثم أراد القضاء في مثله، قال «فخر الإسلام البزدوي » : لا رواية في هذه المسألة، فينبغي أن يجوز قضاؤه في مثله، لأنـه أداها كما وجبت ولا يقضي في مثله على ما قاله « شمس الأئمة»، لأنه لما مضى الوقت صار ديناً ذمته، بصفة الكمال. لأن النقص كان بسبب تغير الوقت، وقد زال فيرتفع النقصان، وتثبت كاملة، في إذ الوجوب في الذمة، ولا نقص في الذمة.
And it is valid to perform what has become obligatory during them (the three times) with dislike, like a funeral that has arrived, and a prostration of a verse recited therein. Similarly, the Asr of the day (performed) at sunset is valid with dislike. And the three times. Benefit: He said in al-Qunyah and others: Common lazy people if they pray Fajr at the time of sunrise, they are not rebuked, because if they are prevented, they would leave it altogether apparently, and if they pray it, it is valid according to the people of hadith, and permissible performance according to some is better than abandonment. And it is valid to perform what has become obligatory in them, i.e., the three times, but with dislike, in the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah), not as some thought who denied it. And he exemplified what becomes obligatory therein by his saying (like a funeral that has arrived). As for the dislike of praying over it, it is due to what preceded of the hadith of Uqbah. And as for validity, due to its obligation by presence. But he said in Mir'aj al-Dirayah from al-Tuhfah: The best in funeral prayer is to perform it when it arrives, due to his saying peace be upon him: 'Three things are not to be delayed' among them the funeral when it arrives. And likewise the prostration of a verse recited in them, i.e., the three times. And a voluntary prayer begun in one of them, or a vowed prayer to be performed in them, is permissible with dislike. And the best is to cut off what one has begun, in the apparent transmission, and make it up in a complete time, because the time for it is a cause of obligation, not a condition for performance; rather performance is obligatory absolutely, so it is not restricted to a time that would cause it to be lost. And it is said: he fulfills his responsibility if he makes it up in a disliked time, though he is sinful, because its obligation is only for the necessity of safeguarding the performed act from nullification, which is achieved despite its deficiency. And it is said: it is not valid to begin voluntarily in them, like obligatory prayers, because the evidence indicates absolute prohibition without lack of validity in some specifically, otherwise it would entail differing meanings of a single word for two intended things not figuratively. (Just as the Asr of the day is valid) by performing it at sunset, due to the survival of its cause, which is the part of time connected to performance (with dislike), due to the prohibited delay, not due to the time itself. And we restricted to Asr of the day, because the Asr of yesterday is not valid when the sun changes on the present day, because the causality is linked to the entire time exiting, and it is not disliked, so it is not performed in a disliked state. And if a disbeliever embraces Islam at yellowing (time of sunset) and did not pray, then wants to make it up in a similar time, Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi said: There is no transmission on this issue, so it should be permissible to make it up in a similar time, because he performed it as it was obligatory. And he does not make it up in a similar time according to what Shams al-A'imma said, because when the time passed it became a debt on his liability with the attribute of perfection. Because the deficiency was due to the change of time, and it has ceased, so the deficiency is removed, and it is established as complete, because obligation is on the liability, and there is no deficiency on the liability.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on performing obligatory prayers during the three prohibited times (sunrise, zenith, sunset). The author begins by stating that it is valid (sahih) to perform what has become obligatory during these times, but with karahah (dislike). Examples given are the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) when the funeral is present, and the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah) when a verse requiring prostration is recited. The author also mentions the current day's Asr prayer if performed near sunset, which is valid with karahah due to delay, not because of the time itself. The passage includes a benefit (fa'idah) from al-Qunyah regarding common people who pray Fajr at sunrise: they should not be rebuked because forbidding them might lead them to abandon the prayer altogether. The ruling is based on the hadith of Uqbah and the principle that the prohibited time makes the act disliked but does not invalidate it because obligatory acts must be performed. The author also discusses a difference of opinion: some say one should cut off a voluntary prayer begun in a prohibited time and make it up later, while others say it is valid but disliked. The passage also addresses the case of a person who embraces Islam near sunset and has missed a prayer; there is no explicit transmission, but some scholars permit making it up in a similar time.

Key Terms
الكراهة (al-karahah): Dislike of a nature that approaches prohibition (karahah tahrimi) in this context, because the act is valid but sinful if done without necessity.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted position from Imam Muhammad's six books; this is the authoritative position of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on performing a funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) during sunrise according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated later.
B) It is valid but makruh tahrimi.
C) It is not permissible under any circumstances.
D) It is recommended to delay it until after sunrise.

Key Takeaway
Obligatory acts like funeral prayer and prostration of recitation are valid even in prohibited times, but they are makruh tahrimi.

Recommended Qualities and Actions of the Muadhdhin
List of recommended qualities and actions for the muadhdhin with proofs and intra-madhhab difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended qualities and actions of the muadhdhin according to the Hanafi school, identify the supporting evidence, and distinguish between obligatory and recommended elements.

Core Idea
The adhan's validity does not depend on the muadhdhin's personal qualities; its excellences are recommended, not required.

The muadhdhin is the caller to prayer, and while the adhan itself has specific conditions for validity, the Sharī‘a encourages certain qualities and actions to enhance its beauty and effectiveness. This passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah lists these mustahabb (recommended) attributes, ranging from personal qualifications like knowledge and wudu to physical actions like facing the qibla and placing fingers in the ears. Understanding these recommendations helps distinguish what is essential for a valid adhan from what is commendable.

Guided Path
1
List the recommended qualities
Identify each recommended quality or action mentioned in the passage: knowledge of Sunnah, knowledge of prayer times, wudu, facing qibla, placing fingers in ears, and the ruling for women's adhan. Note the exception for a rider in travel.
These are mustahabb, not wajib.
2
Categorize the hukm level
The text uses phrases like 'yustahabb' (it is recommended). Confirm that the Hanafi school categorizes these as sunnah/mustahabb, and that omission does not invalidate the adhan.
Compare with conditions (shurut) that are wajib.
3
Examine the proofs
For each recommendation, the author provides a hadith or analogy. Identify the dalil for wudu ('la yu'adhdhin illa mutawaddi') and for placing fingers in ears (Prophet's instruction to Bilal). Note the hadith about choosing the best for adhan.
These are ahad hadith, so they establish recommendation, not obligation.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The passage mentions a difference of opinion regarding adhan while riding in settled areas (hadar). The apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) says it is makruh, but Abu Yusuf says it is permissible without dislike.
This is an example of intra-madhhab variance; the mufta bihi is the disliked view.
5
Recognize the wisdom behind the actions
The commentary explains that placing fingers in ears amplifies the voice. Understanding the rationale (hikmah) helps appreciate why these acts are recommended, such as ensuring the adhan is heard clearly and performed with dignity.
The act is not an original sunna in itself but legislated for a purpose.

عالماً بالسنة، وأوقاتِ الصَّلاةِ، وعلى وضوء، مستقبل القبلة، إلا أن يكون راكباً، و أن يجعل أصبعيه في أذنيه، النساء في صحن الدار أو السطح، وليؤتمن على الأوقات، لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « لِيُؤَكِّنْ لَكُمْ خِيَارُكُمْ، وَلْيَؤْمَكُمْ أقُروكُمْ ) ) . رواه ابن ماجه وأبو داود، (عَالِماً بالسُّنَّة) المتعلقة بالأذان)، ليـأتـي بـه عـلـى وجهها، (و) أن يكون عالماً بعلامات (أوقاتِ الصَّلاةِ، ليأتي به في وقته، فيؤدي النـاس الـعبـادة صحيحة، (و) أن يكون على وضوء ) لقوله : ( لا يُؤذنُ إِلا مُتوضى) (۳) (مُسْتقبل القبلة)؛ كما فعل الملك النازل، إلا أن يكون راكباً) مسافراً، لضرورة السير، لأن بلالاً أذن وهو راكب، ثم نزل، وأقام على الأرض . ويكره الأذان راكباً في الحضر، في ظاهر الرواية ، وعن أبي يوسف: لا بأس به، كما في البدائع». (وَ) يستحب ( أنْ يجعل أصبعيه في أذُنَيْهِ)، لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لبلال : « اجْعَلْ أصبعيـك في أذُنَيك، فإنَّه أرْفَعُ لصوتِكَ » ). وإن جعل يديه على أذنيه فحسن، لأن أبا محذورة له ضم أصابعـه الأربع، ووضعهما على أذنيه. وعن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، أنه إن جعل إحدى يديـه عـلـى أذنيه، فحسن، وإن لم يفعل فالأذان حسن، لأن الفعل ليس سنة أصلية، إذ ليس في أذان صاحب الرؤيا، ولم يشرع إلا لحكمة كونه أرفع للصوت، فيكون أبلغ في الإعلام؛ لأن الصوت يبدأ من مخارج النفس، فإذا سد أذنيه اجتمع النفس في الفم، ويخرج الصوت عالياً من غير ضرورة، ولا يستحب وضع الإصبع في الأذان حال الإقامة، لأنها تكون أخفض من الأذان.
Knowledgeable of the Sunnah, and of the prayer times, and in a state of wudu, facing the qibla, unless he is riding, and to place his two fingers in his ears. Women [should give adhan] in the courtyard or on the roof. And he should be trustworthy regarding the times, because of his saying ﷺ: 'Let your best ones call the iqamah for you, and let your most learned ones lead you in prayer.' Narrated by Ibn Majah and Abu Dawood. (Knowledgeable of the Sunnah) related to the adhan, so that he may perform it in its proper manner. (And) knowledgeable of the signs of the prayer times, so that he may perform it at its time, and thus the people perform the worship correctly. (And) to be in a state of wudu, because of his saying: 'No one should give the adhan except one who is in wudu.' (Facing the qibla) as did the descending angel, unless he is riding and traveling, due to the necessity of journey, because Bilal gave the adhan while riding, then descended and gave the iqamah on the ground. And it is disliked to give the adhan while riding in the settled land (hadar) in the apparent narration. From Abu Yusuf: there is no harm in it, as in al-Bada'i'. (And) it is recommended that he place his two fingers in his ears, because of his saying ﷺ to Bilal: 'Place your two fingers in your ears, for it raises your voice.' And if he places his hands on his ears, it is good, because Abu Mahdhurah used to join his four fingers and place them on his ears. From Abu Hanifa, that if he places one of his hands on his ears, it is good, and if he does not do it, the adhan is good, because the act is not an original sunna, as it is not in the adhan of the one who saw the dream, and it was legislated only for the wisdom of raising the voice, so it becomes more effective in announcement; because the voice emanates from the passages of the breath, so when he blocks his ears, the breath collects in the mouth, and the voice comes out loudly without strain. And it is not recommended to place the finger in the adhan during the iqamah, because it is lower than the adhan.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah enumerates the recommended qualities and actions (mustahabbat) of the muadhdhin (caller to prayer) along with their proofs. The author first lists: being knowledgeable of the Sunnah concerning adhan, knowing the prayer times, being in wudu, facing the qibla (with an exception for a rider in travel), placing the fingers in the ears, and the adhan of women being in the courtyard or roof. The sharh expands each point: knowledge of Sunnah ensures correct performance; knowledge of times ensures timely adhan; wudu is required based on a hadith; facing qibla follows the example of the descending angel; riding is allowed in travel but disliked in settled areas except according to Abu Yusuf. Placing fingers in ears is recommended to amplify voice, based on the Prophet's instruction to Bilal. Alternative methods (hands on ears) are permissible but not original sunna. The text notes that this act is not for iqamah, which is lower in voice. The commentary emphasizes the Hanafi position: the act is not a fundamental sunna but a recommended practice for amplification.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): An action recommended but not obligatory; its omission does not incur sin.
الراكب (al-rakib): One who is riding an animal or vehicle; exception for adhan while riding in travel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a muadhdhin giving adhan while riding in a city (hadar)?
A) Permissible without dislike
B) Disliked in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah)
C) Completely forbidden
D) Obligatory to dismount

Key Takeaway
The adhan's validity is not compromised by omitting recommended acts; they are laudable enhancements, not requirements.

Shart and Rukn: Definitions and Distinctions
Definition and classification of shart and rukn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define shart and rukn as used in Hanafi fiqh, distinguish them based on externality/internality and continuity, classify shart into its three types (rational, legal, contractual), and apply the distinction between shurut jawaz and shurut wujud.

Core Idea
A condition (shart) is external and continuous; a pillar (rukn) is internal and transient — their distinction determines prayer's validity.

This lesson unpacks the foundational terms 'shart' and 'rukn' as defined by the Hanafi school. Understanding these definitions is essential because they govern what makes prayer valid or invalid. The passage presents both linguistic and technical meanings, along with classifications and a key distinction from al-Mabsut that shapes Hanafi fiqh methodology.

Guided Path
1
Extract the key terms
Identify the three terms: shart (condition), rukn (pillar), and fard (obligatory). Note that the text allows 'fard' to be applied to both shart and rukn in a broad sense.
This clarifies that 'fard' in this context is not a technical category but a general descriptor of obligation.
2
Understand the linguistic and technical definitions
Linguistically, shart means a necessary sign (like the signs of the Hour). Technically in Shari'a, it is something external to the essence without which the act cannot exist. Rukn linguistically means a strong side; technically it is the integral part of which the essence is composed.
The key distinction: shart is external (the act depends on it but it is not part of the act), while rukn is internal (part of the act's composition).
3
Classify the types of shart
The text lists three types: rational (e.g., using a tool before carpentry), legal (e.g., purity for prayer), and contractual (e.g., a condition in a contract that suspends a ruling). These are examples of shurut from different domains.
Legal shurut are the ones most relevant to worship; the other two appear in non-ritual contexts.
4
Distinguish between shurut jawaz and shurut wujud
The well-known six conditions of prayer (like facing qibla, covering awra, etc.) are conditions of permissibility (shurut jawaz) – meaning the prayer is not permissible without them. The condition of existence (shart wujud) is the capacity (qudra) that makes the act possible.
This distinction is important because it affects whether an act can be rendered valid despite a missing condition.
5
Apply the continuity criterion from al-Mabsut
According to al-Mabsut, a shart requires continuity throughout the prayer (e.g., purity must persist), while a rukn does not persist – it expires with the commencement of the next rukn. This helps classify each requirement correctly.
For example, standing (qiyam) is a rukn because it ends when you move to bowing; purity is a shart because it must continue throughout.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب شروط الصلاة وأركانها
جمع بينها، وإن أفردوا كلاً بباب على حدة، لأن المقصود علم جميعها لتصحيح الصلاة، فكان الجمع بينهما أظهر في المراد للتيقظ إلى ما تصح به، وفي نسخة شرائط كما عبر به الفقيه «أبو الليث»، وصاحب « منية المصلي». وقال شارحها شرائط جمع شريطة، بمعنى الشرط. انتهى. وكذا في شرح الكنز للديري»، الشريطة في معنى الشرط وجمعها شرائط، وبه يعلم الجواب عن كلام صاحب « البحر» في هذا المحل. انتهى. والشروط جمع شرط، بسكون الراء، والأشراط جمع شرط بفتحها، وهما العلامة، والمستعمل في لسان الفقهاء الشروط دون الأشراط. والشرط في اللغة: العلامة اللازمة، ومنه أشراط الساعة، أي علامتها اللازمة. وفي الشريعة هو: ما يتوقف على وجوده الشيء، وهو خارج عن ماهية الشيء. كذا في غاية البيان ) . وقال «فخر الإسلام»: هو اسم لما يتعلق به الوجود، دون الوجوب، وقيل: ما يسبقه العلة وجوداً، ولا تعمل إلى وجود الشرط. وقد اختلف في تقسيمه، فجعل « أبو زيد» أقسامه أربعة، و «فخر الإسلام البزدوي» خمسة، و«شمس الأئمة السرخسي» ستة، وبعض المحققين إلى قسمين: حقيقة، ومجاز. فالحقيقة ما توجد العلة عند وجوده، أو ما يتوقف المؤثر على وجوده في ثبوت الحكم والمجاز ما عداه، وبقية الأقسام بحسب المجاز لا بحسب الحقيقة، والأركان جمع ركن، وهو في اللغة الجانب الأقوى [ قال تعالى ]: أَوْ ءَاوِى إِلَى رُكْنٍ شَدِيدٍ ﴾ [هود: ۸۰] أي: عز ومنعة، وفي الاصطلاح الجزء الذاتي التي تتركب الماهية منه ومن غيره، ويقال: ما يقوم به الشيء وهو جزء داخل ماهية الشيء، والفرض يجوز إطلاقه على الشطر والركن جميعاً، ثم الشرط على ثلاثة أنواع عقلي: كالقدوم للنجار، وشرعي: كالطهارة للصلاة، وجعلي كالدخول المعلق به الطلاق. وفي ( المبسوط » : حد الشرط: ما يشترط دوامه من أول الصلاة إلى آخرها كالطهارة، وستر العورة وحد الركن ما لا يدوم من أول الصلاة إلى آخرها، بل ينقضي بالشروع في ركن آخر كالقيام والقراءة، كل منهما ينقضي بالركوع، والركوع بالانتقال إلى السجود والشروط الستة شروط جواز لا شروط وجود، وشرط الوجود: القدرة المتصلة بالفعل. وفي هذا الباب شروط متقدمة قبل الدخول في الصلاة ، ومنها التحريمة، وشروط متوسطة، كترتيب الأركان، فيما لم يشرع مكرراً. وقد اتبعت هذه الطريقة تسهيلاً على المتعلم، وإن نظر في
Chapter on the Conditions and Pillars of Prayer. They are combined together, even if some treat each separately in its own chapter, because the purpose is knowledge of all of them for the correctness of prayer, so combining them is more apparent in intent for awareness of what makes it valid. In some copies: 'Shara'it' as expressed by Faqih Abu al-Layth and the author of Munyat al-Musalli. Its commentator said: 'Shara'it is plural of Shariṭa, meaning condition.' End quote. Similarly in Sharh al-Kanz by al-Dayri: 'Shariṭa is in the meaning of shart, plural shara'it, and by this the answer is known regarding the statement of the author of al-Bahr in this context.' End quote. 'Shurut' is plural of 'shart' with sukun on the ra, and 'ashrat' is plural of 'shart' with fatha, and both mean sign/mark. What is used in the language of the jurists is 'shurut' not 'ashrat'. 'Shart' in language: the necessary sign, from it 'ashrat al-sa'a' meaning its necessary signs. In Shari'a: that upon whose existence the thing depends, and it is external to the essence of the thing. This is in Ghayat al-Bayan. Fakhr al-Islam said: it is a name for that to which existence is attached, not obligation. And it is said: what the cause precedes in existence, and the cause does not work to the existence of the condition. There is disagreement in its division: Abu Zaid made it four divisions, Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi five, Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi six, and some verifiers divided into two: real (haqiqa) and metaphorical (majaz). The real is that by whose existence the cause exists, or that upon whose existence the effective cause depends in the establishment of the ruling; the metaphorical is other than that. The remaining divisions are according to metaphorical usage, not real. 'Arkan' is plural of 'rukn', which in language means the strong side. Allah says: 'Or take refuge in a strong support.' i.e. might and protection. In terminology: the essential part from which the essence is composed and from other things. It is said: that by which the thing stands, and it is a part internal to the essence of the thing. It is permissible to apply 'fard' to both the 'shart' and the 'rukn'. Then the condition is of three types: rational, like the adze for the carpenter; legal, like purity for prayer; and contractual, like the entering upon which divorce is suspended. In al-Mabsut: the definition of condition (shart) is that whose continuity is required from the beginning of prayer to its end, like purity and covering the awra. The definition of pillar (rukn) is that which does not continue from the beginning to the end, but rather expires with the commencement of another pillar, like standing and recitation – each of them expires with bowing, and bowing with the transition to prostration. The six conditions are conditions of permissibility (shurut jawaz), not conditions of existence (shurut wujud). The condition of existence (shart wujud) is the ability connected to the action. In this chapter there are conditions that precede entering into prayer, among them the takbir, and intermediate conditions like the order of pillars where repetition is not prescribed. I have followed this method to facilitate the learner, and if one considers...
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the terms 'shart' (condition) and 'rukn' (pillar) within the Hanafi legal tradition. The author begins by explaining why the chapter combines both conditions and pillars: because the objective is to know all the requirements for prayer to be valid. He notes variant terminology: some use 'shara'it' (plural of shariṭa) instead of 'shurut'. The technical definition of shart is given: it is something external to the essence (mahiyya) upon which the existence of the act depends. This distinguishes it from a rukn, which is an integral part of the essence. Several Hanafi authorities are cited: Abu al-Layth, the author of Munyat al-Musalli, al-Dayri, and the author of al-Bahr. The passage then details the linguistic and shar'i definitions. It presents the types of shart: rational (like a carpenter's tool), legal (like purity for prayer), and contractual (like a condition attached to divorce). From al-Mabsut, it defines shart as requiring continuity throughout prayer, while rukn does not persist but is passed when moving to the next pillar. It notes that the six well-known conditions (like facing qibla, covering awra, etc.) are conditions of permissibility (jawaz) not conditions of existence (wujud). The condition of existence is the capacity (qudra) connected to the act. Finally, it mentions that in this chapter, conditions that precede prayer (like takbir) and intermediate conditions (like order of pillars) are covered. This is meant to facilitate learning.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): That upon whose existence the thing depends, and it is external to the essence of the thing. In Hanafi fiqh, it is distinguished from rukn as being external, and from fard as being a condition of permissibility rather than existence.
ركن (rukn): The essential part from which the essence is composed; it is internal to the mahiyya. In prayer, it is an integral that does not persist throughout but is replaced by the next rukn.
فروض (furūḍ): An act that is obligatory, applicable to both shart and rukn in this context. The text says it is permissible to apply 'fard' to both shart and rukn.
شرط جواز (shart jawaz): A condition that makes the act permissible; without it the act is not valid as a legal worship. The six conditions of prayer are of this type.
شرط وجود (shart wujud): The condition that makes the existence of the act possible; e.g., the capacity (qudra) to perform the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of 'shart' (condition) in Islamic law?
A) The essential part from which the essence is composed.
B) That upon whose existence the thing depends, and it is external to the essence.
C) A recommended act that enhances prayer.
D) The strong side or support in a building.

Key Takeaway
Shart is an external, continuous prerequisite; rukn is an internal, transient integral; this distinction governs whether a missing element invalidates an act or can be remedied.

The First Condition of Prayer: Taharah from Hadath
Enumeration of 27 requirements with proof for taharah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first condition of prayer (taharah from hadath) and its proof, and distinguish the intra-Hanafi disagreement on covering wet impurity with a cloth.

Core Idea
Taharah from hadath is the first of 27 obligations for prayer, proven by Quran 5:6 and hadith; a thin cloth over wet impurity is valid only if it can serve as a garment (Muhammad's view).

The author begins the enumeration of the twenty-seven requirements for valid prayer by establishing the first and most fundamental: purity from hadath. This lesson walks through the proof for taharah and the details of removing impurity from the prayer place, including a key intra-Hanafi disagreement on covering wet najasah with a thin cloth. Understanding this condition is crucial because without it, the prayer is invalid, yet its application has subtle nuances that a jurist must grasp.

Guided Path
1
Identify the First Obligation and Its Proof
Locate the statement that purity from hadath (minor, major, menstruation, lochia) is obligatory. Note the Quranic verse (5:6) and the hadith 'The key to prayer is purity' cited as evidence.
The proof is dari (imperative) and qat'i in transmission.
2
Understand the Definition of Hadath
Read the legal definition of hadath: a legal impediment residing in the limbs until removed by its remover (wudu or ghusl). Distinguish it from najasah (impurity of the body/garment/place).
Hadath is a juridical state; najasah is a physical impurity. Both are conditions for prayer.
3
Examine the Ruling on Purity of Place
Analyze the author's rulings on different scenarios: thin cloth over dry impurity, cloth over wet impurity, covering impurity with pure earth, and prayer in a tent with a roof.
The key is that the barrier must effectively separate the worshipper from najasah.
4
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Wet Impurity
Compare the positions of Imam Muhammad (valid if cloth is thick enough to be a garment) and al-Halwani (invalid unless doubled). Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
The dispute centers on what constitutes a sufficient barrier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا بد لصحةِ الصَّلاةِ من سبعة وعشرين شيئاً: الطهارة منَ الحَدَثِ، وطهارة الجسدِ والثَّوبِ ، والمكان .. تقييد « القدوري» شروط بقوله التي تتقدمها، بأنه ليس من الشروط ما لا يكون مقدماً. وشروط الخروج والبقاء على الصحة، ليسا شرطين للصلاة، بل لأمر آخر، وهـو : الخروج والبقاء علـى الصحة، فلا يرد علينا، لأنا قيدنا بما يميز كلاً عن غيره فيما سيأتي، وقال في « البدرية » : هذا القيد، أي: قيد القدوري، قصدي لا اتفاقي، لأنه ذكر في باب شروط الصلاة الشروط المتقدمة دون الشروط المتوسطة، كترتيب الأركان فيما لم يشرع مكرراً .انتهى فلذا قلت لا بدَّ لصحةِ الصَّلاةِ من وجود (سبعة وعشرين شيئاً) من المصلي، والشيء يصدق بالركن وبالشرط الذي لا بد منه لصحة الشروع في الصلاة، وبما هو شرط لبقائها على الصحة، وقد بيناه فيما سيأتي مفصلاً، وكلها فروض، وحصرناها بهذا العد تقريباً لا تحقيقاً، لأنه يزاد عليها، واقتصار بعضهم على ذكر الشروط الستة والأركان فيه قصور فمن الفروض ( الطَّهارة منَ الحَدَثِ الأصغر والأكبر والحيض والنفاس، لآيــة الطهارة)، وقوله : ( مفتاح الصلاةِ الطَّهور » (۳). وتقدم صفة التطهر وشرطه، والحدث لغة: الشيء الحادث، وشرعاً: مانعية شرعية قائمة بالأعضاء إلى غاية وصول المزيل لها، وقدم الشروط لأنها لا تسقط بحال، ولا يرد مسألة مقطوع اليدين والرجلين ومجروح الوجه، إذ يصلـي بـلا طهارة، لأنـه نادر، ولا حكم له، ولا يرد الوقت لأنه من الشروط التكليفية، فلا يكلف بالمفروض إلا بوجوده، والاستقبال للخائف ونحوه جهة قدرته، فلم يسقط الاستقبال في الجملة، (و) يفترض (طهارة الجسد، و( يفترض طهارة ( الثَّوبِ، وَ) طهارة (المَكَانِ) الذي يصلي عليه، فلو بسط شيئاً رقيقاً علــى موضع نجس، جاف وصلى عليه إن كان بحال يصلح ساتراً للعورة، تجوز الصلاة، وإن كانت النجاسة رطبة، فألقى عليها لبداً (۳) أو ثوباً، وصلى إن كان ثوباً، يمكن أن يجعل من ثخنه ثوباً، يجوز عند محمد، وإن كان لا يمكن لا يجوز. وقال « الحلواني» : لا يجوز حتى يلقي على هذا الطرف الطرف الآخر، فيصير بمنزلة ثوبين، وإن كبسها بالتراب الطاهر، فلم يوجد ريح النجاسة، جازت الصلاة عليها، وإذا صلى في خيمة، وصار سقفها على رأسه لتمام قيامه، جاز إن كانت طاهرة وإلا فلا، ولو كان في يده حبل مربوط بنجاسة، إن سقط على الأرض، ولم يتحرك بحركته صحت صلاته،
For the validity of prayer, twenty-seven things are necessary: purity from hadath, purity of the body, of the garment, and of the place... The restriction of al-Quduri: conditions by his statement 'those that precede it' - because there is no condition that is not preceded. The conditions for exiting and remaining in validity are not conditions for prayer, but for something else: exiting and remaining in validity. So it does not apply to us, because we have restricted [conditions] to what distinguishes each from others in what will come. It is said in al-Badriyya: this restriction, i.e. al-Quduri's restriction, is intentional not coincidental, because he mentioned in the chapter on conditions of prayer the conditions that precede, not the intermediate conditions, like the order of pillars where repetition is not prescribed. End quote. Therefore I said: It is necessary for the validity of prayer from the existence of twenty-seven things from the one praying. And 'thing' applies to the pillar and to the condition that is necessary for the validity of commencing prayer, and to what is a condition for its remaining valid. We will explain it in detail in what follows. All of them are fard (obligatory). We have limited them to this count approximately, not exactly, because more can be added. Some merely mentioning the six conditions and pillars is deficient. So from the obligatory duties is: purity from minor hadath, major hadath, menstruation, and post-partum bleeding, due to the verse of taharah, and his statement: 'The key to prayer is purity.' The description of purification and its condition have preceded. 'Hadath' linguistically: an occurring thing; legally: a legal impediment residing in the limbs until the time of reaching its remover. Conditions have been mentioned first because they do not fall away under any circumstance. The case of one who has no hands, feet, or face is not considered, for he prays without purification, but it is rare and has no ruling. Time is not considered because it is a condition of obligation (shart taklifi), so one is not obligated except with its existence. Facing the qibla for the one in fear and the like is according to his ability, so facing the qibla is not completely waived. And it is obligatory (yuf'tarad) purity of the body, purity of the garment, and purity of the place upon which one prays. So if one spreads a thin thing over a dry impure place and prays on it, if it is such that it can act as a cover for the awra, then the prayer is valid. If the impurity is wet, and he throws a felt [padding] or a cloth over it, and prays – if it is a cloth that can be made from its thickness into a garment, it is permissible according to Muhammad; if not, it is not permissible. Al-Halwani said: it is not permissible until he throws one side over the other, making it like two garments. If he covers it with pure earth and no smell of impurity remains, prayer upon it is valid. If he prays in a tent and its roof is above his head due to his standing, it is valid if [the roof] is pure, otherwise not. If a rope tied to impurity is in his hand, and it falls to the ground without moving due to his movement, his prayer is valid.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and it begins the enumeration of the twenty-seven things required for prayer's validity. The author first states the matn of Nur al-Idah that 27 things are necessary, beginning with purity from hadath, then purity of body, garment, and place. He then discusses the restriction of al-Quduri, who limits 'conditions' in the chapter on prayer conditions to those that precede prayer, excluding intermediate conditions like the order of pillars. The author defends this restriction, citing al-Badriyya that it is intentional. He then reiterates the 27 things and explains that they include both conditions and pillars (rukn), since 'thing' applies to both. All are considered fard (obligations). He then elaborates on the first obligation: purity from hadath (both minor and major, including menstruation and lochia) with the proof from the Quranic verse of wudu (Quran 5:6) and the hadith 'The key to prayer is purity' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud). He defines 'hadath' legally as a legal impediment in the limbs until removed. He notes that conditions are mentioned before pillars because they do not fall away under any circumstance. He then discusses exceptional cases: a person with amputated limbs may pray without purity, but this is rare and not a basis for ruling. Time is a condition of obligation (taklifi), not of performance. Facing qibla is not waived entirely; for those in fear, it is according to ability. Then he details the purity of body, garment, and place. He gives several rulings: if a thin cloth is spread over dry najasah and it can serve as a cover for awra, prayer is valid. If the najasah is wet, a thick cloth that can itself be considered a garment is permissible per Imam Muhammad; if not, it is not. Al-Halwani holds it is not permissible unless the cloth is doubled. Covering with pure earth to remove smell permits prayer. A tent's roof must be pure for prayer to be valid. A rope tied to impurity does not affect prayer if it falls without moving due to the person's movement.

Key Terms
حدث (ḥadath): A legal impediment residing in the limbs until removed (by wudu or ghusl). It makes prayer invalid without purification.
طهارة (ṭahārah): Purity from hadath and najasah (impurity). It is the first condition of prayer.
نجاسة (najāsah): Impurity (like urine, blood) that must be removed from body, garment, and place for prayer validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Prayer is valid always.
B) Prayer is valid according to Muhammad if the cloth can be considered a garment; otherwise not.
C) Prayer is invalid according to all Hanafi scholars.
D) Prayer is valid only if the impurity is dry.

Key Takeaway
Taharah from hadath is the first of 27 obligations for valid prayer, proven by the Quran and hadith, and the purification of place includes nuanced rulings on barriers against impurity.

Purity of Place: The Hanafi Conditions for Valid Prayer
Detailed exposition of the requirement of purity of place for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that the place of prayer (including the forehead, hands, knees, and feet) must be free from unforgiven impurity, and apply the ruling to scenarios involving transitional movement or wet impurity on the ground.

Core Idea
The place of each limb used in prostration must be pure; even a brief stay on impurity during a rukn invalidates the prayer.

This lesson unpacks a critical section from the commentary on Nur al-Idah regarding the twenty-seven conditions for prayer, with a special focus on the requirement that the place where one prays be pure from najasah (impurity). The text not only states the rule but also provides detailed scenarios involving wet and dry impurity, transitional movement during prayer, and the purity of individual limbs (feet, hands, knees, forehead). As a ruling-with-proof passage, it anchors each obligation in Quran and hadith while addressing divergent opinions within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall ruling
Recognise that the passage declares purity of body, clothing, and place as obligatory (fard) conditions for prayer. Note that all twenty-seven items are fard, not just the famous six.
The text emphasises that these are conditions (shurut) that precede the prayer.
2
Distinguish between dry and wet impurity
Read the scenarios: dry impurity can be covered with a thin cloth; wet impurity requires a thicker covering. Note the difference between Muhammad and al-Halwani.
The precautionary view (al-Halwani) is taken in fatwa.
3
Analyse the transition case
Study the dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: if a person moves from a pure to an impure spot during prayer and stays for the duration of a rukn without performing it. Apply the chosen view (Abu Yusuf) that it invalidates.
The text explicitly says 'al-mukhtar qawl Abi Yusuf'.
4
Examine the requirement for the limbs of prostration
Note that the place of the feet, hands, knees, and forehead must be pure. The sound view is that impurity on any of these invalidates the prayer. The contrary narration is considered anomalous.
The basis is the hadith of prostrating on seven bones.
5
Apply the dirham rule
Understand that if each foot has less than a dirham of impurity but combined they exceed, the prayer is invalid. Also, if one foot is on pure ground and the other on impurity, the prayer is valid but disliked.
The combination rule shows careful Hanafi quantification.

عَنْهُ)، و تقدم بيانه) (حَتَّى) أنه يشترط طهارة (موضعِ القَدَمَيْنِ)، فلو وضع واحدة منهما على نجس مانع، لا تصح صلاته على الأصح؛ لأن فرض القيام تأدى بهما مع استصحاب النجاسة، فلا تصح الصلاة، وإن وضع واحدة فقط على طهارة، ورفع الأخرى، تأدى بها الفرض، فصحت الصلاة، وكره لترك وضع الأخرى، وإن كان تحت كل واحد أقل من قدر الدرهم، وإذا جمع زاد عليه، لا تصح في الأصح، لأن القيام يضاف إليهما فانعدم للنجاسة المانعة، وإن افتتح الصلاة على مكان طاهر، ثم انتقل على مكان نجس، ولم يمكث مقدار ركن صحت صلاته اتفاقاً، لأن المكث اليسير على النجس الكثير، كالمكث الكثير مع النجس القليل معفو عنه، وإن مكث عليه مقدار ركن من غير أدائه فسدت، عند أبي يوسف وقال محمد: جازت والمختار قول أبي يوسف، احتياطاً كما لو أدى ركنـاً مـع المكـث وحكـم الانكشاف كذلك. (و) يشترط طهارة موضع ( اليدين و) موضـــع ( الرُّكْبَتَيْن) على الصحيح. واختاره الفقيه « أبو الليث»، لافتراض السجود على سبعة أعظم، والوضع على النجاسة كلا ،وضع فكأنه لم يسجد، فتفسد، وحكم الواحدة منهما كحكـم إحدى الرجلين. وما قيل من عدم افتراض طهارة موضعهما ينكره الفقيه ( أبو الليث»، وعليـه بـنـي وجـوب وضع الركبتين في السجود، ورواية جواز الصلاة مع نجاسة موضع الكفين والركبتين شاذة، (وَ) يشترط طهارة موضع (الجبهة، على الأصح من الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة، وهو قولهما ليتحقق السجود عليها، لأن الفرض وإن كان يتأدى بمقدار الأرنبة ) على القول المرجوح، ولكن إذا وضع الجبهة مع الأرنبة يقع الكل فرضاً، كما إذا طول القراءة على القدر المفروض، وينعدم السجود بالوضع على المكان النجس، ولا يصح ولو أعاده على طاهر في ظاهر الرواية.
It is necessary for the validity of prayer twenty-seven things: purity from hadath, purity of the body, clothing, and place. Al-Quduri restricted the conditions with his statement 'which precede it' such that nothing that is not preceding is a condition. Conditions of exiting and remaining upon validity are not conditions for prayer, but for another matter. He said in al-Badriyya: This restriction is intentional not accidental, because he mentioned in the chapter of conditions of prayer the preceding conditions without the intermediate conditions. Therefore I said: It is necessary for the validity of prayer the existence of twenty-seven things from the worshipper, and 'thing' applies to pillar and to condition necessary for beginning prayer and for remaining upon validity. All are obligations. This enumeration is approximate, not exact, because more could be added. From the obligations: purity from minor and major hadath, menses and postpartum bleeding, due to the verse of purity and his saying: 'The key to prayer is purification.' The description and condition of purification have preceded. Hadath linguistically means something occurring; legally: a legal preventer inherent in the limbs until the arrival of that which removes it. These conditions are presented because they never drop. The case of one with amputated hands and feet or a wounded face is not considered, because such is rare and has no ruling. Time is not objected because it is a conditioning obligation. Facing the qibla for the fearful is according to his ability, so facing the qibla is not dropped entirely. And purity of the body is obligatory, purity of the clothing is obligatory, and purity of the place where one prays is obligatory. If one spreads a thin cloth over a dry impure place and prays upon it, provided it is suitable to cover the awrah, the prayer is permissible. If the impurity is wet and one throws a felt or garment upon it and prays, if the garment can be made into a thick garment, it is permissible according to Muhammad; otherwise not. Al-Halwani said: It is not permissible until one throws the other end over it, making it like two garments. If one covers it with pure soil so that no odor of impurity remains, prayer upon it is permissible. If one prays in a tent and its ceiling is on his head for the completion of his standing, it is permissible if it is pure, otherwise not. If he has in his hand a rope tied to an impurity that falls to the ground and does not move with his movement, his prayer is valid even if the impurity is not forgiven, until the place of the feet, hands, knees, and forehead according to the most sound view. If it moves with his movement but not due to attachment to him, like a turban whose impure end is thrown while the pure end remains on his head, it is valid. We will mention it. If a child sits in the lap of the worshipper while holding on, and there is much impurity on his body or clothing, or if a ritually impure bird sits on the worshipper's head, his prayer is valid as long as no unforgiven impurity transfers to him, because the condition is that the body, clothing, and place are free from unforgiven impurity. Its explanation has preceded. So even the place of the feet is required to be pure. If one places one foot on a preventing impurity, his prayer is not valid according to the most sound view, because the obligation of standing is fulfilled by both feet while carrying the impurity, so the prayer is not valid. If he places only one on a pure place and lifts the other, the obligation is fulfilled by that one, so the prayer is valid, but it is disliked to leave the other unplaced. If under each foot there is less than a dirham of impurity but combined it exceeds, the prayer is not valid in the most sound view, because standing is attributed to both feet, so it is nullified by the preventing impurity. If he begins prayer on a pure place then moves to an impure place and does not stay for the duration of a rukn, his prayer is valid by agreement, because a short stay on much impurity is like a long stay with little impurity, which is forgiven. If he stays on it for the duration of a rukn without performing the rukn, it becomes invalid according to Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said it is permissible, and the chosen view is that of Abu Yusuf, as a precaution, just as if he performed a rukn while staying. The ruling of exposure is similar. And purity of the place of the hands and the place of the knees is required according to the sound view. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth chose this, because prostration is prescribed on seven bones, and placing on impurity is like not placing, so it would invalidate. The ruling of one of them is like the ruling of one foot. The statement that purity of their place is not obligatory is rejected by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, and upon this is built the obligation of placing the knees in prostration. The narration permitting prayer with impurity on the place of the palms and knees is anomalous. And purity of the place of the forehead is required according to the most sound of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa, which is the view of the two companions, to realize prostration upon it, because even though the obligation may be fulfilled by [the nose], according to the weak view, when one places the forehead with the nose, the whole becomes obligatory, as when one lengthens the recitation beyond the obligatory amount. Prostration is nullified by placing on an impure place, and it is not valid even if he repeats it on a pure place in the apparent narration.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling-with-proof exposition from the commentary on Nur al-Idah, focusing on the conditions (shurut) for the validity of prayer. The author begins by stating that prayer requires twenty-seven things, all of which are obligations (fard). He clarifies that conditions are only those that precede prayer, distinguishing them from conditions of exit or remaining. The primary condition discussed is purification (taharah), supported by the Quranic verse (al-Ma'idah 5:6) and the hadith 'The key to prayer is purification.' The passage then breaks down the required purities: from hadath (ritual impurity), and from najasah (impurity) on the body, clothing, and place. A series of scenarios illustrate the rulings: if one spreads a thin cloth over dry impurity, prayer is valid if the cloth covers the awrah; for wet impurity, there is a difference between Muhammad (who allows if the cloth is thick enough to serve as a proper covering) and al-Halwani (who requires two layers). Using pure soil to cover the impurity is permissible if no odor remains. Prayer in a tent requires the ceiling to be pure if it touches the head. A rope tied to impurity that lies on the ground without moving does not invalidate prayer, but if it moves with the worshipper's motion, it is like the turban case: valid if the impure part is away. A child with impurity on his clothes or a impure bird on the head does not invalidate prayer unless unforgiven impurity transfers. The author then specifies that the place of the feet, hands, knees, and forehead must be pure. For the feet: if one foot is on impurity and the other on pure ground, prayer is valid but disliked; if both feet have less than a dirham each but combined exceed, prayer is invalid. If a worshipper moves from a pure to impure spot during prayer, brief stay (less than a rukn) is forgiven; staying for a rukn invalidates according to Abu Yusuf (the preferred view), while Muhammad allows it. The hands and knees: the sound view requires their purity, based on the hadith of prostrating on seven bones; a contrary narration is considered anomalous. The forehead: the most sound narration from Abu Hanifa and the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require purity of the forehead's place; even if one repeats the prostration on a pure spot, the prayer is not valid in the apparent narration. The commentary emphasizes that these are all obligatory conditions (fard) and that careful attention to purity of the place of prostration is essential for valid prayer.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity, either minor (hadas asghar) or major (hadas akbar), that prevents prayer until removed.
نجاسة (najasah): Impurity (filth) on the body, clothing, or place that is not forgiven; must be removed or covered for prayer to be valid.
شرط (shart): A condition whose absence invalidates the act; here, conditions that precede prayer (shurut qabliyyah).
ركن (rukn): A pillar or integral part of prayer; omission invalidates the prayer entirely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person is standing in prayer with one foot on a pure place and the other foot on a impure place, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is valid but disliked (makruh).
B) The prayer is invalid because one foot is on impurity.
C) The prayer is valid and not disliked.
D) The prayer is invalid unless the impurity is less than a dirham.

Key Takeaway
The place of each limb of prostration (feet, hands, knees, forehead) must be free from unforgiven impurity; a brief stay on impurity during a rukn invalidates the prayer per the preferred Hanafi view.

Purity of the Seven Limbs in Prostration
Explains the requirement of purity for the seven limbs of prostration with detailed scenarios and a dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the requirement for purity of the seven limbs in prostration and apply the Hanafi rulings to cases involving impurity on these limbs.

Core Idea
Prostration requires purity of all seven contact points; any unexcused impurity on them invalidates the prayer.

In this passage, the commentator explains that for prayer to be valid, the places where the seven limbs touch the ground during prostration must be free of unexcused impurity. The text covers the feet, hands, knees, and forehead, with special cases and an intra-madhhab dispute regarding staying on an impure spot.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling
Recognize that purity of the seven limbs is a condition (shart) for the validity of prayer, based on the hadith commanding prostration on seven bones.
The condition applies to the place of each limb.
2
Analyze the Scenarios for the Feet
Work through the cases: one foot on impure ground, lifting a foot to avoid impurity, and combined impurity under both feet.
Combined impurity exceeding a dirham invalidates prayer even if each individually is excused.
3
Understand the Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Examine the difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on staying on an impure spot for the duration of a rukn.
Abu Yusuf invalidates the prayer; Muhammad considers it valid. The chosen view is Abu Yusuf's for precaution.
4
Apply the Ruling to Hands, Knees, and Forehead
Note that the correct view requires purity for these limbs as well, rejecting the anomalous narration that exempts palms and knees.
The forehead's purity is especially emphasized, with the nose being a secondary part.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
Conclude that the relied-upon position is that of Abu Yusuf: staying on impurity for a rukn invalidates the prayer, and purity of all limbs is obligatory.
The fatwa follows the stricter view to ensure validity.

Source Text

(و) يشترط طهارة موضع ( اليدين و) موضـــع ( الرُّكْبَتَيْن) على الصحيح. واختاره الفقيه « أبو الليث»، لافتراض السجود على سبعة أعظم، والوضع على النجاسة كلا ،وضع فكأنه لم يسجد، فتفسد، وحكم الواحدة منهما كحكـم إحدى الرجلين. وما قيل من عدم افتراض طهارة موضعهما ينكره الفقيه ( أبو الليث»، وعليـه بـنـي وجـوب وضع الركبتين في السجود، ورواية جواز الصلاة مع نجاسة موضع الكفين والركبتين شاذة، (وَ) يشترط طهارة موضع (الجبهة، على الأصح من الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة، وهو قولهما ليتحقق السجود عليها، لأن الفرض وإن كان يتأدى بمقدار الأرنبة ) على القول المرجوح، ولكن إذا وضع الجبهة مع الأرنبة يقع الكل فرضاً، كما إذا طول القراءة على القدر المفروض، وينعدم السجود بالوضع على المكان النجس، ولا يصح ولو أعاده على طاهر في ظاهر الرواية.
Najāsah that is not excused is required (to be absent), even (from) the place of the two feet, the two hands, the two knees, and the forehead, according to the most correct (view). And he may move by his movement without connection to it, like the turban whose impure end is thrown and the pure part remains on his head, it is valid. And we will mention it. And if a child sits in the lap of the prayer, while holding on, and there is much najāsah on his body or clothes, or an impure bird sits on the head of the prayer, his prayer is permissible, if nothing of the najāsah that is not excused separates to him; because the condition is that the body, clothing, and place are free from najāsah that is not excused, and its explanation preceded. (Even to the extent that) purity is required for the place of the two feet: if he places one of them on impure (ground) that prevents, his prayer is not valid according to the most correct (view); because the duty of standing is fulfilled by both while continuing the najāsah, so the prayer is not valid. And if he places only one on pure (ground) and lifts the other, the duty is fulfilled by it, so the prayer is valid, and it is disliked to leave the other. And if under each is less than a dirham’s amount, and when combined it exceeds that, it is not valid according to the most correct (view), because standing is attributed to both, so it is nullified by the preventing najāsah. And if he begins prayer on a pure place, then moves to an impure place, and does not stay the duration of a rukn, his prayer is valid by agreement, because a brief stay on much najāsah is like a long stay with little najāsah, it is excused. And if he stays on it for the duration of a rukn without performing it, it is invalid according to Abū Yūsuf, and Muḥammad said: it is valid. The chosen (position) is the saying of Abū Yūsuf, as a precaution, just as if he performed a rukn while staying. And the ruling of uncovering is likewise. And purity of the place of the two hands and the place of the two knees is required according to the correct (view). Al-Faqīh Abu al-Layth chose it, because prostration is obligatory on seven bones, and placing on najāsah is like not placing, so it is as if he did not prostrate, thus it invalidates. The ruling of one of them is like the ruling of one of the two feet. And what is said about purity of their place not being obligatory is denied by al-Faqīh Abu al-Layth, and upon it is based the obligation of placing the knees in prostration. And the narration permitting prayer with najāsah on the place of the palms and knees is anomalous. And purity of the place of the forehead is required, according to the most correct of the two narrations from Abū Ḥanīfah, and it is the saying of the two (Ṣāḥibayn) to verify prostration upon it, because although the duty is fulfilled by the amount of the arabeh (tip of the nose) according to the weaker opinion, but when he places the forehead along with the arabeh, all becomes duty, just as if he lengthens the recitation beyond the obligatory amount. And prostration is nullified by placing on an impure place, and it is not valid even if he repeats it on a pure (place) according to the apparent narration.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah (Sharh Nur al-Idah) discusses the requirement for purity of the seven limbs that touch the ground in prostration. It begins by stating that the places of the feet, hands, knees, and forehead must be free of ritual impurity (najāsah) that is not excused (i.e., more than a dirham in area). The author then clarifies that if a movable impurity is attached (like a turban with a clean part on the head), it is permissible. Then the focus shifts to the feet: if one foot is placed on an impure spot, the prayer is invalid because the duty of standing (qiyam) is performed with both feet. However, if only one foot is on pure ground and the other is lifted, the prayer is valid (though disliked). A crucial point: if under each foot there is less than a dirham's area of impurity, but combined it exceeds that, the prayer is invalid. Next, the passage addresses moving to an impure spot during prayer: if the prayer stays only briefly (less than one rukn), the prayer remains valid. But if he stays for the duration of one rukn, there is a dispute: Abu Yusuf says invalid (and this is the chosen view for precaution), while Muhammad says valid. The hands and knees: their purity is required according to the correct view, relying on the hadith of seven limbs. The forehead: the most correct view, which is also the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), is that its purity is required, because prostration is on the forehead. If only the nose touches impurity while the forehead is pure, the prayer is valid by agreement (since the nose is less than a dirham). The key principle: the condition is absence of unc excused impurity on the body, clothing, and place of prostration.

Key Terms
أرنبة (aranabah): The tip of the nose (or the soft part).
معفو عنه (ma'fu 'anhu): Impurity that is excused, typically less than a dirham in area (about diameter of a coin).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Yes, valid but disliked
B) No, invalid
C) Yes, and not disliked
D) Only valid if the lifted foot is also pure

Key Takeaway
The purity of all seven limbs of prostration is a condition for valid prayer; any unexcused impurity on them, especially if combined or prolonged, can invalidate the prayer.

Qibla for the Non-Sighted in Mecca: Direction vs Exact Kaaba
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qibla obligation for non-sighted in Mecca

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between tahqiq and taqrib in qibla, and apply the ruling that a non-sighted person in Mecca may face the direction (jiha) rather than the exact Kaaba.

Core Idea
When facing the distant Kaaba, a small deviation does not break alignment — thus the non-sighted need only face its direction, not its exact structure.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about qibla for a person in Mecca who cannot see the Kaaba. Using a geometric analogy of distant vs near facing, Hanafi scholars conclude that the non-sighted person's obligation is to face the direction (jiha), not the exact Kaaba. We will trace the rational argument and the supporting authorities from the text.

Guided Path
1
Understand Tahqiq and Taqrib
The passage defines exact facing (tahqiq) as a line from the face passing directly over the Kaaba at a right angle, and approximate facing (taqrib) as a deviation that still leaves some part of the face aligned. Grasp these technical terms as they are the foundation of the dispute.
Tahqiq is the ideal; taqrib is the acceptable range.
2
Follow the Rational Analogy of Distance
When facing something close, a small shift eliminates facing; when far, a large shift is needed. Since Mecca is far from most lands, a wide arc of orientations counts as facing. This analogy supports the direction view.
This is the core dalil aqli.
3
Identify the Authorities and Positions
Al-Zandawisati's hierarchy (Kaaba → Masjid → Mecca → Haram → world) implies that only those in the Masjid see the Kaaba. Al-Hidayah states that the sighted must face the exact Kaaba; the non-sighted must face direction. Ibn al-Humam raises an objection about climbing mountains for certainty.
The chosen view (al-mukhtar) is direction.
4
Apply the Ruling to a Practical Scenario
If a blind person in Mecca prays at home facing what he believes is the qibla, and later discovers the Kaaba was behind him, according to the mufta bihi view his prayer is valid because he fulfilled the obligation of jiha.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو بمكة، على الصحيح.
(r)
ومعنى التحقيق: أنه لو فُرض خطّ من تلقاء وجهه على زاوية قائمة إلى الأفق يـكـون مـاراً عـلـى الكعبة، أو هو ائها، ومعنى التقريب أن يكون ذلك منحرفاً عن الكعبة أو هوائها انحرافاً لا تزول به المقابلة الكلية بأن يبقى شيء من سطح الوجه مسامتاً لها أو لهوائها، وبيانه: أن مقابلة الشيء بالشيء إذا وقعت في مسافة قريبة تزول بانتقال قليل من اليمين أو الشمال مناسب لتلك المسافة، وإذا وقعت في مسافة بعيدة لا تزول بمثل ذلك الانتقال، بل بانتقال مناسب لذلك البعد، فإن إنساناً لو قابل إنساناً في مسافة ذراع ) مثلاً تزول تلك المقابلة بانتقال أحدهما بمقدار ذراع أو نحوها، وإذا وقعت المقابلة بينهما في مقدار ميل أو فرسخ ، لا تزول تلك المقابلة إلا بمقدار مئة ذراع أو نحوها، بل يحتاج في زوال المقابلة إلى مسافة بعيدة مناسبة لذلك البعد على ما عرف تحقيقه في موضعه، ثم إن مكة لما بعدت عن ديارنا بعداً مفرطاً، تتحقق المقابلة إليها في مواضع كثيرة في مسافة بعيدة، فإنا لو فرضنا خطاً من تلقاء وجه مستقبل الكعبة على التحقيق في هذه البلاد، ثـم فرضنا خطاً آخر يقطع ذلك الخط على زاويتين قائمتين من جانب يمين المستقبل وشماله، لا تزول تلك المقابلة والتوجه بالانتقال إلى اليمين والشمال عن ذلك الخط بفراسخ كثيرة، ولذلك وضع العلماء قبلة بلاد متقاربة على سمت واحد. انتهى. إذا علمت ما ذكرناه، فالفرض لغير المشاهد إصابة جهتها، (وَلَوْ ) كان غير المشاهد ( بِمَكَّةَ)، وحال بينه وبين الكعبـة بنـاء أو جبل (علـى الصحيح). قال في «معراج الدراية ) : ولمن كان بمكة وبينه وبين الكعبة حائل يمنــع كالأبينية، فالأصح أن حكمه حكم الغائب، ولو كان الحائل أصلياً كالجبل فله أن يجتهد، والأولى أن يصعد على الجبل حتى تكون صلاته إلى الكعبة يقيناً. انتهى. وذكر ( الزندويستي، رحمه الله في نظمه أن الكعبة قبلة من يصلي في المسجد الحرام والمسجد الحرام قبلة أهل مكة لمن يصلي ببيته أو في البطحاء ) ، ومكة قبلة أهل الحرم، والحرم قبلة أهل العالم، قال صاحب « الهدايــة» في التجنيس والمزيد : وهذا يشير إلى أن من كان بمعاينة الكعبة فالشرط إصابة عينها، ومن لم يكن بمعاينتها فالشرط إصابة جهتها، وهو المختار. انتهى. وقال الشيخ عبد العزيز البخاري : هذا على التقريب، وإلا فالتحقيق أن الكعبة قبلة .العالم. انتهى. وقال ( الكمال بن الهمام : وعندي في جواز التحري مع إمكان صعوده أي صعود المكي الجبل إشكال، لأن المصير، إلى الدليل الظني، وترك القاطع مع إمكانه لا يجوز، وما أقرب قوله في الكتاب والاستخبار فوق التحري، فإذا امتنع
وقد فاز من حاز هذا البسط، إذ لا يمل.
And even if in Mecca, on the correct view. And the meaning of exact facing (tahqiq): if a line is assumed from in front of his face at a right angle to the horizon passing over the Kaaba or its airspace. And the meaning of approximate facing (taqrib): that it deviates from the Kaaba or its airspace in such a way that complete facing is not eliminated, so that some part of the surface of the face remains aligned with it or its airspace. Explanation: facing something with something when at a short distance is eliminated by a slight movement to the right or left proportionate to that distance; when at a great distance, it is not eliminated by such movement but by movement proportionate to that distance. For if a person faces another at a distance of a cubit, that facing is eliminated by one of them moving about a cubit; if the distance is a mile or a farsakh, it is not eliminated except by about a hundred cubits; rather, elimination of facing requires a great distance proportionate to that as known. Then since Mecca is extremely far from our lands, facing it is realized in many places over a great distance. So if we assume a line from the face of one facing the Kaaba exactly in these lands, then assume another line intersecting that line at right angles to the right and left of the one facing, that facing and orientation is not eliminated by moving right and left many farsakhs. Therefore, scholars set one direction for near lands. End. Then if you understood what we mentioned, the obligation for the non-sighted is to face its direction, (even if) the non-sighted (in Mecca) with a building or mountain (blocking) (on the correct view). He said in Ma'raj al-Diraya: For one in Mecca with a blocking barrier like buildings, the correct view is that his ruling is the same as the absent one; if the barrier is natural like a mountain, he may exert ijtihad, but it is better to climb the mountain so his prayer faces the Kaaba with certainty. End. He mentioned al-Zandawisati in his poem that the Kaaba is the qibla for one praying in the Sacred Mosque, and the Sacred Mosque is the qibla for the people of Mecca who pray at home or in al-Batha, and Mecca is the qibla for the sanctuary, and the sanctuary is the qibla for the whole world. The author of al-Hidayah said: This indicates that for one who sees the Kaaba, the condition is facing its exact self; for one who does not see it, the condition is facing its direction, and that is the chosen view. End. And Shaykh Abd al-Aziz al-Bukhari said: This is approximate; otherwise, the reality is that the Kaaba is the qibla of the world. End. And Kamal Ibn al-Humam said: In my view, there is a problem with permitting ijtihad for the Meccan to climb a mountain, because resorting to a presumptive proof while abandoning certainty when possible is not permissible; but his statement in the book 'and inquiry is above ijtihad' so when it is prevented...
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the qibla obligation for a person in Mecca who cannot see the Kaaba due to a barrier. The commentary begins by explaining the technical terms tahqiq (exact facing) and taqrib (approximate facing) with a rational analogy: when objects are close, a small shift eliminates facing; when far, a large shift is needed. Since Mecca is far from distant lands, facing the direction suffices over a wide area. The ruling states that for the non-sighted, the obligation is to face the direction (jiha), even if in Mecca, on the correct view (al-sahih). The author then quotes several authorities: Ma'raj al-Diraya says the non-sighted in Mecca with a building blocking is like an absent person; if the barrier is natural (mountain), ijtihad is allowed but climbing is better for certainty. Al-Zandawisati's poem hierarchically assigns qibla: Kaaba for those in Masjid al-Haram, Masjid for Meccans at home, Mecca for sanctuary, sanctuary for world. Al-Hidayah endorses the distinction: sighted must face the exact Kaaba, non-sighted face direction – this is the chosen view (al-mukhtar). Al-Bukhari clarifies that this taqrib is practical, but in reality the Kaaba is qibla for all. Ibn al-Humam raises an objection: ijtihad (relying on zann) is problematic if certainty (yaqin) is possible by climbing; he finds this problematic. The passage concludes that the absent person's obligation is direction. This shows the Hanafi school's nuanced approach: while the exact Kaaba is the qibla in principle, practical necessity allows direction for those who cannot ascertain it.

Key Terms
التحقيق (al-taḥqīq): Exact facing: when the line from the face passes directly over the Kaaba or its airspace at a right angle.
التقريب (al-taqrīb): Approximate facing: when the deviation from the Kaaba is not so great that complete facing is lost; some part of the face remains aligned.
مقابلة (muqābala): The act of facing something; in this context, the geometric alignment of the person's orientation with the Kaaba.
جهة (jiha): Direction; the approximate orientation considered sufficient for qibla when exact facing is impossible.
غير المشاهد (ghayr al-mushāhid): The non-sighted person; one who does not see the Kaaba directly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the qibla obligation for a person in Mecca who cannot see the Kaaba due to a building?
A) He must face the exact Kaaba with certainty.
B) He must climb a mountain to see the Kaaba.
C) He must face the direction (jiha) of the Kaaba.
D) He may pray without qibla.

Key Takeaway
For the non-sighted in Mecca, the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling requires only facing the direction (jiha) of the Kaaba, not the exact building, based on a rational analogy of facing at distances.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Conditions for Valid Fard Prayer
Expounds the two conditions for valid fard prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two alternative conditions for the validity of fard prayer and determine whether a given scenario of ignorance invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
You needn't know every fard and sunnah within a prayer—just that the prayer itself is fard.

In this passage from Imdad al-Fattah, the commentator clarifies what is necessary for a valid obligatory prayer. Rather than requiring detailed knowledge of each component, the valid conditions ensure the worshipper does not mistakenly perform a supererogatory act with the intention of obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two alternative conditions
The commentator states that for a fard prayer to be valid, the worshipper must either (a) know the manner of the prayer in a way that distinguishes it as obligatory from supererogatory, or (b) believe that all the rak'ahs he prays are obligatory.
2
Explain what each condition means
The first condition requires knowing the specific prayer (e.g., Fajr) is fard, even if one doesn't know which internal parts are fard. The second condition is that the worshipper believes all rak'ahs he performs are fard, which suffices because supererogatory can be intended as fard.
The second condition relies on the principle that supererogatory acts can be fulfilled with the intention of obligatory, but not vice versa.
3
Apply to the case of total ignorance
If a person prays the five prayers without knowing they are obligatory, his prayer is invalid because he did not intend fard. Similarly, if he knows some are fard and some sunnah but cannot distinguish, his prayer is invalid unless he follows an imam.
The exception: following an imam suffices because the intention is to pray with the imam, not necessarily to distinguish.
4
Distinguish between knowing external status and internal details
It is not required to know which parts of a single prayer are fard (e.g., standing is a pillar, recitation is fard, etc.). Knowing the prayer itself is fard is sufficient.
Example: It suffices to know that Fajr prayer is fard, even if one thinks standing is sunnah.
5
Apply to the imam leading a congregation
If an imam does not know fard from sunnah but intends the whole prayer as fard, his own prayer is valid. However, for the congregation, prayers that have no sunnah before them ( 'Asr, Maghrib, 'Isha) are valid, but prayers with a preceding sunnah (Fajr, Zuhr) are not, because the imam's intention would include the sunnah rak'ahs as fard, which is invalid.
